*float64\n   334→}\n   335→\n   336→// Visitor allows visiting a Node and its child nodes. If the visitor w returned by\n// v.Visit(node, path) is not nil and the visitor returns no error, Walk is\n// invoked recursively with visitor w for each of the non-nil children of node,\n// followed by a call of w.Visit(nil), returning an error\n// As the tree is descended the path of previous nodes is provided.\nfunc Walk(v Visitor, node Node, path []Node) error {\n\tvar err error\n\tif v, err = v.Visit(node, path); v == nil || err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\tvar pathToHere []Node // Initialized only when needed.\n\n\tfor e := range ChildrenIter(node) {\n\t\tif pathToHere == nil {\n\t\t\tpathToHere = append(path, node)\n\t\t}\n\t\tif err := Walk(v, e, pathToHere); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t_, err = v.Visit(nil, nil)\n\treturn err\n}\n\nfunc ExtractSelectors(expr Expr) [][]*labels.Matcher {\n\tvar selectors [][]*labels.Matcher\n\tInspect(expr, func(node Node, _ []Node) error {\n\t\tvs, ok := node.(*VectorSelector)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\tselectors = append(selectors, vs.LabelMatchers)\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn nil\n\t})\n\treturn selectors\n}\n\ntype inspector func(Node, []Node) error\n\nfunc (f inspector) Visit(node Node, path []Node) (Visitor, error) {\n\tif err := f(node, path); err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, err\n\t}\n\n\treturn f, nil\n}\n\n// Inspect traverses an AST in depth-first order: It starts by calling\n// f(node, path); node must not be nil. parser.\n   359→// It writes the next Item provided by the lexer to the provided pointer address.\n   360→// Comments are skipped.\n   361→//\n   362→// The yyLexer interface is currently implemented by the parser to allow\n   363→// the generated and non-generated parts to work together with regards to lookahead\n   364→// and error handling.\n   365→//\n   366→// For more information, see 372→\t\treturn int(p.inject)\n   373→\t}\n   374→\t// Skip comments.\n   375→\tfor {\n   376→\t\tp.lex.NextItem(&lval.item)\n   377→\t\ttyp = lval.item.Typ\n   378→\t\tif typ != COMMENT {\n   379→\t\t\tbreak\n   380→\t\t}\n   381→\t}\n   382→\n   383→\tswitch typ {\n   384→\tcase ERROR:\n   385→\t\tpos := posrange.PositionRange{\n   386→\t\t\tStart: p.lex.start,\n   387→\t\t\tEnd: 0\n   393→\tcase EOF:\n   394→\t\tlval.item.Typ = EOF\n   395→\t\tp.InjectItem(0)\n   396→\tcase RIGHT_BRACE, RIGHT_PAREN, RIGHT_BRACKET, DURATION, NUMBER:\n   397→\t\tp.lastClosing = lval.item.Pos + 405→// It is a no-op since the parsers error routines are triggered\n   406→// by mechanisms that allow more fine-grained control\n   407→// For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\n   408→func (*parser) Error(string) {\n   409→}\n   410→\n   411→// InjectItem allows injecting a single Item at the beginning of the token stream\n https://www.gnu.org/software/bison/manual/html_node/Multiple-start_002dsymbols.html .\n   415→// Only the Lex function used by the generated parser is affected by this injected Item.\n   416→// Trying and must be enabled with --enable-feature=promql-experimental-functions\", ret.Op)\n   483→\t\t\treturn ret\n   484→\t\t}\n   485→\t\tdesiredArgs = 2\n   486→\n   487→\t\tret.Param = arguments[0]\n   488→\t}\n   489→\n   490→\tif len(arguments) != desiredArgs {\n   491→\t\tp.addParseErrf(ret.PositionRange(), \"wrong number of arguments for aggregate expression provided, expected %d, got %d\", desiredArgs, len(arguments))\n   492→\t\treturn ret\n   493→\t}\n   494→\n   495→\tret.Expr = arguments[desiredArgs-1]\n   496→\n   497→\treturn ret\n   498→}\n   499→\n   500→// newMap is used when building the FloatHistogram from a map.\n   501→func (*parser) newMap() (ret map[string]any) {\n   502→\treturn map[string]any{}\n   503→}\n   504→\n   505→// mergeMaps is used to combine maps as they're used to later build the Float histogram.\n   506→// This will merge the right map into the left map.\n   507→func (p *parser) mergeMaps(left, right *map[string]any) (ret *map[string]any) {\n   508→\tfor key, value := range *right {\n   509→\t\tif _, ok := (*left)[key]; ok {\n   510→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(posrange.PositionRange{}, \"duplicate key \\\"%s\\\" in histogram\", key)\n   511→\t\t\tcontinue\n   512→\t\t}\n   513→\t\t(*left)[key] = value\n   514→\t}\n   515→\treturn left\n   516→}\n   517→\n   518→func (p *parser) histogramsIncreaseSeries(base, inc *histogram.FloatHistogram, times uint64) ([]SequenceValue, error) {\n   519→\t// Capture the hint set flag immediately after inc histogram is built.\n   520→\t// The base histogram's hint set flag was already captured.\n   521→\thintSet := p.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet\n   522→\treturn p.histogramsSeries(base, inc, times, hintSet, func(a, b *histogram.FloatHistogram) (*histogram.FloatHistogram, error) {\n   523→\t\tres, _, _, err := a.Add(b)\n   524→\t\treturn res, err\n   525→\t})\n   526→}\n   527→\n   528→func (p *parser) histogramsDecreaseSeries(base, inc *histogram.FloatHistogram, times uint64) ([]SequenceValue, error) {\n   529→\t// Capture the hint set flag immediately after inc histogram is built.\n   530→\thintSet := p.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet\n   531→\treturn p.histogramsSeries(base, inc, times, hintSet, func(a, b *histogram.FloatHistogram) (*histogram.FloatHistogram, error) {\n   532→\t\tres, _, _, err := a.Sub(b)\n   533→\t\treturn res, err\n   534→\t})\n   535→}\n   536→\n   537→func (*parser) histogramsSeries(base, inc *histogram.FloatHistogram, times uint64, counterResetHintSet bool,\n   538→\tcombine func(*histogram.FloatHistogram, *histogram.FloatHistogram) (*histogram.FloatHistogram, error),\n   539→) ([]SequenceValue, error) {\n   540→\tret := make([]SequenceValue, times+1)\n   541→\t// Add an additional value (the base) for time 0, which we ignore in tests.\n   542→\tret[0] = SequenceValue{Histogram: base, CounterResetHintSet: counterResetHintSet}\n   543→\tcur := base\n   544→\tfor i := uint64(1); i <= times; i++ {\n   545→\t\tif cur.Schema > inc.Schema {\n   546→\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"error combining histograms: cannot merge from schema %d to %d\", inc.Schema, cur.Schema)\n   547→\t\t}\n   548→\n   549→\t\tvar err error\n   550→\t\tcur, err = combine(cur.Copy(), inc)\n   551→\t\tif err != nil {\n   552→\t\t\treturn ret, err\n   553→\t\t}\n   554→\t\tret[i] = SequenceValue{Histogram: cur, CounterResetHintSet: counterResetHintSet}\n   555→\t}\n   556→\n   557→\treturn ret, nil\n   558→}\n   559→\n   560→// buildHistogramFromMap is used in the grammar to take then individual parts of the histogram and complete it.\n   561→func (p *parser) buildHistogramFromMap(desc *map[string]any) *histogram.FloatHistogram {\n   562→\toutput := &histogram.FloatHistogram{}\n   563→\t// Reset the flag for each new histogram being built.\n   564→\tp.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet = false\n   565→\n   566→\tval, ok := (*desc)[\"schema\"]\n   567→\tif ok {\n   568→\t\tschema, ok := val.(int64)\n   569→\t\tif ok {\n   570→\t\t\toutput.Schema = int32(schema)\n   571→\t\t} else {\n   572→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing schema number: %v\", val)\n   573→\t\t}\n   574→\t}\n   575→\n   576→\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"sum\"]\n   577→\tif ok {\n   578→\t\tsum, ok := val.(float64)\n   579→\t\tif ok {\n   580→\t\t\toutput.Sum = sum\n   581→\t\t} else {\n   582→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing sum number: %v\", val)\n   583→\t\t}\n   584→\t}\n   585→\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"count\"]\n   586→\tif ok {\n   587→\t\tcount, ok := val.(float64)\n   588→\t\tif ok {\n   589→\t\t\toutput.Count = count\n   590→\t\t} else {\n   591→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing count number: %v\", val)\n   592→\t\t}\n   593→\t}\n   594→\n   595→\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"z_bucket\"]\n   596→\tif ok {\n   597→\t\tbucket, ok := val.(float64)\n   598→\t\tif ok {\n   599→\t\t\toutput.ZeroCount = bucket\n   600→\t\t} else {\n   601→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing z_bucket number: %v\", val)\n   602→\t\t}\n   603→\t}\n   604→\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"z_bucket_w\"]\n   605→\tif ok {\n   606→\t\tbucketWidth, ok := val.(float64)\n   607→\t\tif ok {\n   608→\t\t\toutput.ZeroThreshold = bucketWidth\n   609→\t\t} else {\n   610→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing z_bucket_w number: %v\", val)\n   611→\t\t}\n   612→\t}\n   613→\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"custom_values\"]\n   614→\tif ok {\n   615→\t\tcustomValues, ok := val.([]float64)\n   616→\t\tif ok {\n   617→\t\t\toutput.CustomValues = customValues\n   618→\t\t} else {\n   619→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing custom_values: %v\", val)\n   620→\t\t}\n   621→\t}\n   622→\n   623→\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"counter_reset_hint\"]\n   624→\tif ok {\n   625→\t\t// Mark that the counter reset hint was explicitly specified.\n   626→\t\tp.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet = true\n   627→\t\tresetHint, ok := val.(Item)\n   628→\n   629→\t\tif ok {\n   630→\t\t\tswitch resetHint.Typ {\n   631→\t\t\tcase UNKNOWN_COUNTER_RESET:\n   632→\t\t\t\toutput.CounterResetHint = histogram.UnknownCounterReset\n   633→\t\t\tcase COUNTER_RESET:\n   634→\t\t\t\toutput.CounterResetHint = histogram.CounterReset\n   635→\t\t\tcase NOT_COUNTER_RESET:\n   636→\t\t\t\toutput.CounterResetHint = histogram.NotCounterReset\n   637→\t\t\tcase GAUGE_TYPE:\n   638→\t\t\t\toutput.CounterResetHint = histogram.GaugeType\n   639→\t\t\tdefault:\n   640→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing counter_reset_hint: unknown value %v\", resetHint.Typ)\n   641→\t\t\t}\n   642→\t\t} else {\n   643→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing counter_reset_hint: %v\", val)\n   644→\t\t}\n   645→\t}\n   646→\n   647→\tbuckets, spans := p.buildHistogramBucketsAndSpans(desc, \"buckets\", \"offset\")\n   648→\toutput.PositiveBuckets = buckets\n   649→\toutput.PositiveSpans = spans\n   650→\n   651→\tbuckets, spans = p.buildHistogramBucketsAndSpans(desc, \"n_buckets\", \"n_offset\")\n   652→\toutput.NegativeBuckets = buckets\n   653→\toutput.NegativeSpans = spans\n   654→\n   655→\treturn output\n   656→}\n   657→\n   658→// newHistogramSequenceValue creates a SequenceValue for a histogram,\n   659→// setting CounterResetHintSet based on whether counter_reset_hint was\n   660→// explicitly specified in the histogram description.\n   661→func (p *parser) newHistogramSequenceValue(h *histogram.FloatHistogram) SequenceValue {\n   662→\treturn SequenceValue{\n   663→\t\tHistogram:           h,\n   664→\t\tCounterResetHintSet: p.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet,\n   665→\t}\n   666→}\n   667→\n   668→func (p *parser) buildHistogramBucketsAndSpans(desc *map[string]any, bucketsKey, offsetKey string,\n   669→) (buckets []float64, spans []histogram.Span) {\n   670→\tbucketCount := 0\n   671→\tval, ok := (*desc)[bucketsKey]\n   672→\tif ok {\n   673→\t\tval, ok := val.([]float64)\n   674→\t\tif ok {\n   675→\t\t\tbuckets = val\n   676→\t\t\tbucketCount = len(buckets)\n   677→\t\t} else {\n   678→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing %s float array: %v\", bucketsKey, val)\n   679→\t\t}\n   680→\t}\n   681→\toffset := int32(0)\n   682→\tval, ok = (*desc)[offsetKey]\n   683→\tif ok {\n   684→\t\tval, ok := val.(int64)\n   685→\t\tif ok {\n   686→\t\t\toffset = int32(val)\n   687→\t\t} else {\n   688→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing %s number: %v\", offsetKey, val)\n   689→\t\t}\n   690→\t}\n   691→\tif bucketCount > 0 {\n   692→\t\tspans = []histogram.Span{{Offset: offset, Length: uint32(bucketCount)}}\n   693→\t}\n   694→\treturn buckets, spans\n   695→}\n   696→\n   697→// number parses a number.\n   698→func (p *parser) number(val string) float64 {\n   699→\tn, err := strconv.ParseInt(val, 0, 64)\n   700→\tf := float64(n)\n   701→\tif err != nil {\n   702→\t\tf, err = strconv.ParseFloat(val, 64)\n   703→\t}\n   704→\tif err != nil {\n   705→\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing number: %s\", err)\n   706→\t}\n   707→\treturn f\n   708→}\n   709→\n   710→// expectType checks the type of the node and raises an error if it\n   711→// is not of the expected type.\n   712→func (p *parser) expectType(node Node, want ValueType, context string) {\n   713→\tt := p.checkAST(node)\n   714→\tif t != want {\n   715→\t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"expected type %s in %s, got %s\", DocumentedType(want), context, DocumentedType(t))\n   716→\t}\n   717→}\n   718→\n   719→// checkAST checks the validity of the provided AST. This includes type checking.\n   720→func (p *parser) checkAST(node Node) (typ ValueType) {\n   721→\t// For expressions the type is determined by their Type function.\n   722→\t// Lists do not have a type but are not invalid either.\n   723→\tswitch n := node.(type) {\n   724→\tcase Expressions:\n   725→\t\ttyp = ValueTypeNone\n   726→\tcase Expr:\n   727→\t\ttyp = n.Type()\n   728→\tdefault:\n   729→\t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"unknown node type: %T\", node)\n   730→\t}\n   731→\n   732→\t// Recursively check correct typing for child nodes and raise\n   733→\t// errors in case of bad typing.\n   734→\tswitch n := node.(type) {\n   735→\tcase *EvalStmt:\n   736→\t\tty := p.checkAST(n.Expr)\n   737→\t\tif ty == ValueTypeNone {\n   738→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.Expr.PositionRange(), \"evaluation statement must have a valid expression type but got %s\", DocumentedType(ty))\n   739→\t\t}\n   740→\n   741→\tcase Expressions:\n   742→\t\tfor _, e := range n {\n   743→\t\t\tty := p.checkAST(e)\n   744→\t\t\tif ty == ValueTypeNone {\n   745→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(e.PositionRange(), \"expression must have a valid expression type but got %s\", DocumentedType(ty))\n   746→\t\t\t}\n   747→\t\t}\n   748→\tcase *AggregateExpr:\n   749→\t\tif !n.Op.IsAggregator() {\n   750→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"aggregation operator expected in aggregation expression but got %q\", n.Op)\n   751→\t\t}\n   752→\t\tp.expectType(n.Expr, ValueTypeVector, \"aggregation expression\")\n   753→\t\tif n.Op == TOPK || n.Op == BOTTOMK || n.Op == QUANTILE || n.Op == LIMITK || n.Op == LIMIT_RATIO {\n   754→\t\t\tp.expectType(n.Param, ValueTypeScalar, \"aggregation parameter\")\n   755→\t\t}\n   756→\t\tif n.Op == COUNT_VALUES {\n   757→\t\t\tp.expectType(n.Param, ValueTypeString, \"aggregation parameter\")\n   758→\t\t}\n   759→\n   760→\tcase *BinaryExpr:\n   761→\t\tlt := p.checkAST(n.LHS)\n   762→\t\trt := p.checkAST(n.RHS)\n   763→\n   764→\t\t// opRange returns the PositionRange of the operator part of the BinaryExpr.\n   765→\t\t// This is made a function instead of a variable, so it is lazily evaluated on demand.\n   766→\t\topRange := func() (r posrange.PositionRange) {\n   767→\t\t\t// Remove whitespace at the beginning and end of the range.\n   768→\t\t\tfor r.Start = n.LHS.PositionRange().End; isSpace(rune(p.lex.input[r.Start])); r.Start++ {\n   769→\t\t\t}\n   770→\t\t\tfor r.End = n.RHS.PositionRange().Start - 1; isSpace(rune(p.lex.input[r.End])); r.End-- {\n   771→\t\t\t}\n   772→\t\t\treturn r\n   773→\t\t}\n   774→\n   775→\t\tif n.ReturnBool && !n.Op.IsComparisonOperator() {\n   776→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"bool modifier can only be used on comparison operators\")\n   777→\t\t}\n   778→\n   779→\t\tif n.Op.IsComparisonOperator() && !n.ReturnBool && n.RHS.Type() == ValueTypeScalar && n.LHS.Type() == ValueTypeScalar {\n   780→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"comparisons between scalars must use BOOL modifier\")\n   781→\t\t}\n   782→\n   783→\t\tif n.Op.IsSetOperator() && n.VectorMatching.Card == CardOneToOne {\n   784→\t\t\tn.VectorMatching.Card = CardManyToMany\n   785→\t\t}\n   786→\n   787→\t\tfor _, l1 := range n.VectorMatching.MatchingLabels {\n   788→\t\t\tfor _, l2 := range n.VectorMatching.Include {\n   789→\t\t\t\tif l1 == l2 && n.VectorMatching.On {\n   790→\t\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"label %q must not occur in ON and GROUP clause at once\", l1)\n   791→\t\t\t\t}\n   792→\t\t\t}\n   793→\t\t}\n   794→\n   795→\t\tif !n.Op.IsOperator() {\n   796→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"binary expression does not support operator %q\", n.Op)\n   797→\t\t}\n   798→\t\tif lt != ValueTypeScalar && lt != ValueTypeVector {\n   799→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.LHS.PositionRange(), \"binary expression must contain only scalar and instant vector types\")\n   800→\t\t}\n   801→\t\tif rt != ValueTypeScalar && rt != ValueTypeVector {\n   802→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.RHS.PositionRange(), \"binary expression must contain only scalar and instant vector types\")\n   803→\t\t}\n   804→\n   805→\t\tswitch {\n   806→\t\tcase (lt != ValueTypeVector || rt != ValueTypeVector) && n.VectorMatching != nil:\n   807→\t\t\tif len(n.VectorMatching.MatchingLabels) > 0 {\n   808→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"vector matching only allowed between instant vectors\")\n   809→\t\t\t}\n   810→\t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.FillValues.LHS != nil || n.VectorMatching.FillValues.RHS != nil {\n   811→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"filling in missing series only allowed between instant vectors\")\n   812→\t\t\t}\n   813→\t\t\tn.VectorMatching = nil\n   814→\t\tcase n.Op.IsSetOperator(): // Both operands are Vectors.\n   815→\t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.Card == CardOneToMany || n.VectorMatching.Card == CardManyToOne {\n   816→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"no grouping allowed for %q operation\", n.Op)\n   817→\t\t\t}\n   818→\t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.Card != CardManyToMany {\n   819→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"set operations must always be many-to-many\")\n   820→\t\t\t}\n   821→\t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.FillValues.LHS != nil || n.VectorMatching.FillValues.RHS != nil {\n   822→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"filling in missing series not allowed for set operators\")\n   823→\t\t\t}\n   824→\t\t}\n   825→\n   826→\t\tif (lt == ValueTypeScalar || rt == ValueTypeScalar) && n.Op.IsSetOperator() {\n   827→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"set operator %q not allowed in binary scalar expression\", n.Op)\n   828→\t\t}\n   829→\n   830→\tcase *Call:\n   831→\t\tnargs := len(n.Func.ArgTypes)\n   832→\t\tif n.Func.Variadic == 0 {\n   833→\t\t\tif nargs != len(n.Args) {\n   834→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"expected %d argument(s) in call to %q, got %d\", nargs, n.Func.Name, len(n.Args))\n   835→\t\t\t}\n   836→\t\t} else {\n   837→\t\t\tna := nargs - 1\n   838→\t\t\tif na > len(n.Args) {\n   839→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"expected at least %d argument(s) in call to %q, got %d\", na, n.Func.Name, len(n.Args))\n   840→\t\t\t} else if nargsmax := na + n.Func.Variadic; n.Func.Variadic > 0 && nargsmax < len(n.Args) {\n   841→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"expected at most %d argument(s) in call to %q, got %d\", nargsmax, n.Func.Name, len(n.Args))\n   842→\t\t\t}\n   843→\t\t}\n   844→\n   845→\t\tif n.Func.Name == \"info\" && len(n.Args) > 1 {\n   846→\t\t\t// Check the type is correct first\n   847→\t\t\tif n.Args[1].Type() != ValueTypeVector {\n   848→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"expected type %s in %s, got %s\", DocumentedType(ValueTypeVector), fmt.Sprintf(\"call to function %q\", n.Func.Name), DocumentedType(n.Args[1].Type()))\n   849→\t\t\t}\n   850→\t\t\t// Check the vector selector in the input doesn't contain a metric name\n   851→\t\t\tif vs, ok := n.Args[1].(*VectorSelector); ok && vs.Name != \"\" {\n   852→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.Args[1].PositionRange(), \"expected label selectors only, got vector selector instead\")\n   853→\t\t\t} else if ok {\n   854→\t\t\t\t// Set Vector Selector flag to bypass empty matcher check\n   855→\t\t\t\tvs.BypassEmptyMatcherCheck = true\n   856→\t\t\t} else {\n   857→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.Args[1].PositionRange(), \"expected label selectors only\")\n   858→\t\t\t}\n   859→\t\t}\n   860→\n   861→\t\tfor i, arg := range n.Args {\n   862→\t\t\tif i >= len(n.Func.ArgTypes) {\n   863→\t\t\t\tif n.Func.Variadic == 0 {\n   864→\t\t\t\t\t// This is not a vararg function so we should not check the\n   865→\t\t\t\t\t// type of the extra arguments.\n   866→\t\t\t\t\tbreak\n   867→\t\t\t\t}\n   868→\t\t\t\ti = len(n.Func.ArgTypes) - 1\n   869→\t\t\t}\n   870→\t\t\tif t := p.checkAST(arg); t != n.Func.ArgTypes[i] {\n   871→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(arg.PositionRange(), \"expected type %s in call to function %q, got %s\", DocumentedType(n.Func.ArgTypes[i]), n.Func.Name, DocumentedType(t))\n   872→\t\t\t}\n   873→\t\t}\n   874→\n   875→\tcase *ParenExpr:\n   876→\t\tp.checkAST(n.Expr)\n   877→\n   878→\tcase *UnaryExpr:\n   879→\t\tif n.Op != ADD && n.Op != SUB {\n   880→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"only + and - operators allowed for unary expressions\")\n   881→\t\t}\n   882→\t\tif t := p.checkAST(n.Expr); t != ValueTypeScalar && t != ValueTypeVector {\n   883→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"unary expression only allowed on expressions of type scalar or instant vector, got %q\", DocumentedType(t))\n   884→\t\t}\n   885→\n   886→\tcase *SubqueryExpr:\n   887→\t\tty := p.checkAST(n.Expr)\n   888→\t\tif ty != ValueTypeVector {\n   889→\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"subquery is only allowed on instant vector, got %s instead\", ty)\n   890→\t\t}\n   891→\tcase *MatrixSelector:\n   892→\t\tp.checkAST(n.VectorSelector)\n   893→\n   894→\tcase *VectorSelector:\n   895→\t\tif n.Name != \"\" {\n   896→\t\t\t// In this case the last LabelMatcher is checking for the metric name\n   897→\t\t\t// set outside the braces. This checks if the name has already been set\n   898→\t\t\t// previously.\n   899→\t\t\tfor _, m := range n.LabelMatchers[0 : len(n.LabelMatchers)-1] {\n   900→\t\t\t\tif m != nil && m.Name == labels.MetricName {\n   901→\t\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"metric name must not be set twice: %q or %q\", n.Name, m.Value)\n   902→\t\t\t\t}\n   903→\t\t\t}\n   904→\n   905→\t\t\t// Skip the check for non-empty matchers because an explicit\n   906→\t\t\t// metric name is a non-empty matcher.\n   907→\t\t\tbreak\n   908→\t\t}\n   909→\t\tif !n.BypassEmptyMatcherCheck {\n   910→\t\t\t// A Vector selector must contain at least one non-empty matcher to prevent\n   911→\t\t\t// implicit selection of all metrics (e.g. by a typo).\n   912→\t\t\tnotEmpty := false\n   913→\t\t\tfor _, lm := range n.LabelMatchers {\n   914→\t\t\t\tif lm != nil && !lm.Matches(\"\") {\n   915→\t\t\t\t\tnotEmpty = true\n   916→\t\t\t\t\tbreak\n   917→\t\t\t\t}\n   918→\t\t\t}\n   919→\t\t\tif !notEmpty {\n   920→\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"vector selector must contain at least one non-empty matcher\")\n   921→\t\t\t}\n   922→\t\t}\n   923→\n   924→\tcase *NumberLiteral, *StringLiteral:\n   925→\t\t// Nothing to do for terminals.\n   926→\n   927→\tdefault:\n   928→\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"unknown node type: %T\", node)\n   929→\t}\n set to true when the most recently\n\t// built histogram had a counter_reset_hint explicitly specified.\n\t// This is used to populate CounterResetHintSet in = opts\n\n\t// Clear lexer struct before reusing.\n\tp.lex = Lexer{\n\t\tinput: input,\n\t\tstate: lexStatements,\n\t}\n\n\treturn p\n}\n\n// newParserWithFunctions returns a new low-level parser p\n}\n\nfunc (p *parser) parseExpr() (expr Expr, err error) {\n\tdefer p.recover(&err)\n\n\tparseResult := p.parseGenerated(START_EXPRESSION)\n\n\tif parseResult != nil {\n\t\texpr = e.Err)\n}\n\ntype ParseErrors []ParseErr\n\n// Since producing multiple error messages might look weird when combined with error wrapping,\n// only the first error produced by the parser is included in the error string.\n// If getting the full error list is desired, it is recommended to typecast the error returned\n// by the parser to ParseErrors and work with the underlying slice.\nfunc (errs ParseErrors) Error() string {\n\tif len(errs) != 0 {\n\t\treturn errs[0].Error()\n\t}\n\t// Should never happen\n\t// Panicking while printing an error seems like a bad idea, so the\n\t// situation is explained in the error message instead.\n\treturn \"error contains no error message\"\n}\n\n// EnrichParseError enriches a single or list of parse errors (used for unit tests and promtool).\nfunc always the last item produced\n// by the lexer.\nfunc (p *parser) unexpected(context, expected string) {\n\tvar errMsg strings.Builder\n\n\t// Do not report lexer errors twice\n\tif p.yyParser.lval.item.Typ == ERROR {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\terrMsg.WriteString(\"unexpected \")\n\terrMsg.WriteString(p.yyParser.lval.item.desc())\n\n\tif context != \"\" {\n\t\terrMsg.WriteString(\" in \")\n\t\terrMsg.WriteString(context)\n\t}\n\n\tif expected != \"\" {\n\t\terrMsg.WriteString(\", expected \")\n\t\terrMsg.WriteString(expected)\n\t}\n\n\tp.addParseErr(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), errors.New(errMsg.String()))\n}\n\nvar errUnexpected = errors.New(\"unexpected error\")\n\n// recover is the handler that turns panics into returns from the top level of Parse.\nfunc (*parser) recover(errp *error) {\n\te := recover()\n\tswitch _, ok := e.(runtime.Error); {\n\tcase ok:\n\t\t// Print the stack trace but do not inhibit the running application.\n\t\tbuf := make([]byte, 64<<10)\n\t\tbuf = buf[:runtime.Stack(buf, false)]\n\n\t\tfmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, \"parser panic: %v\\n%s\", e, buf)\n\t\t*errp = errUnexpected\n\tcase e != nil:\n\t\t*errp = e.(error)\n\t}\n}\n\n// Lex is expected by the yyLexer interface of the yacc generated parser.\n// It writes the next Item provided by the lexer to the provided pointer address.\n// Comments are skipped.\n//\n// The yyLexer interface is currently implemented by the parser to allow\n// the generated and non-generated parts to work together with regards to lookahead\n// and error handling.\n//\n// For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\nfunc (p *parser) Lex(lval *yySymType) int {\n\tvar typ ItemType\n\n\tif p.injecting {\n\t\tp.injecting = false\n\t\treturn int(p.inject)\n\t}\n\t// Skip comments.\n\tfor {\n\t\tp.lex.NextItem(&lval.item)\n\t\ttyp = lval.item.Typ\n\t\tif typ != COMMENT {\n\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tswitch typ {\n\tcase ERROR:\n\t\tpos := posrange.PositionRange{\n\t\t\tStart: p.lex.start,\n\t\t\tEnd:   posrange.Pos(len(p.lex.input)),\n\t\t}\n\t\tp.addParseErr(pos, errors.New(p.yyParser.lval.item.Val))\n\n\t\t// Tells yacc that this is the end of input.\n\t\treturn 0\n\tcase EOF:\n\t\tlval.item.Typ = EOF\n\t\tp.InjectItem(0)\n\tcase RIGHT_BRACE, RIGHT_PAREN, RIGHT_BRACKET, DURATION, NUMBER:\n\t\tp.lastClosing = lval.item.Pos + posrange.Pos(len(lval.item.Val))\n\t}\n\n\treturn int(typ)\n}\n\n// Error is expected by the yyLexer interface of the yacc generated parser.\n//\n// It is a no-op since the parsers error routines are triggered\n// by mechanisms that allow more fine-grained control\n// For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\nfunc (*parser) Error(string) {\n}\n\n// InjectItem allows injecting a single Item at the beginning of the token stream\n// consumed by the generated parser.\n// This allows having multiple start symbols as described in\n// https://www.gnu.org/software/bison/manual/html_node/Multiple-start_002dsymbols.html .\n// Only the Lex function used by the generated parser is affected by this injected Item.\n// Trying to inject when a previously injected Item has not yet been consumed will panic.\n// Only Item types that are supposed to be used as start symbols are allowed as an argument.\nfunc (p *parser) InjectItem(typ ItemType) {\n\tif p.injecting {\n\t\tpanic(\"cannot inject multiple Items into the token stream\")\n\t}\n\n\tif typ != 0 && (typ <= startSymbolsStart || typ >= startSymbolsEnd) {\n\t\tpanic(\"cannot inject symbol that isn't start symbol\")\n\t}\n\n\tp.inject = typ\n\tp.injecting = true\n}\n\nfunc (p *parser) newBinaryExpression(lhs Node, op Item, modifiers, rhs Node) *BinaryExpr {\n\tret := modifiers.(*BinaryExpr)\n\n\tret.LHS = lhs.(Expr)\n\tret.RHS = rhs.(Expr)\n\tret.Op = op.Typ\n\n\tif !p.options.EnableBinopFillModifiers && (ret.VectorMatching.FillValues.LHS != nil || ret.VectorMatching.FillValues.RHS != nil) {\n\t\tp.addParseErrf(ret.PositionRange(), \"binop fill modifiers are experimental and not enabled\")\n\t\treturn ret\n\t}\n\n\treturn ret\n}\n\nfunc (*parser) assembleVectorSelector(vs *VectorSelector) {\n\t// If the metric name was set outside the braces, add a matcher for it.\n\t// If the metric name was inside the braces we don't need to do anything.\n\tif vs.Name != \"\" {\n\t\tnameMatcher, err := labels.NewMatcher(labels.MatchEqual, labels.MetricName, vs.Name)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tpanic(err) // Must not happen with labels.MatchEqual\n\t\t}\n\t\tvs.LabelMatchers = append(vs.LabelMatchers, nameMatcher)\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (p *parser) newAggregateExpr(op Item, modifier, args Node, overread bool) (ret *AggregateExpr) {\n\tret = modifier.(*AggregateExpr)\n\targuments := args.(Expressions)\n\n\tret.PosRange = posrange.PositionRange{\n\t\tStart: op.Pos,\n\t\tEnd:   p.lastClosing,\n\t}\n\tif overread {\n\t\tret.PosRange.End = p.lex.findPrevRightParen(p.lastClosing)\n\t}\n\n\tret.Op = op.Typ\n\n\tif len(arguments) == 0 {\n\t\tp.addParseErrf(ret.PositionRange(), \"no arguments for aggregate expression provided\")\n\n\t\t// Prevents invalid array accesses.\n\t\treturn ret\n\t}\n\n\tdesiredArgs := 1\n\tif ret.Op.IsAggregatorWithParam() {\n\t\tif !p.options.EnableExperimentalFunctions && ret.Op.IsExperimentalAggregator() {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(ret.PositionRange(), \"%s() is experimental and must be enabled with --enable-feature=promql-experimental-functions\", ret.Op)\n\t\t\treturn ret\n\t\t}\n\t\tdesiredArgs = 2\n\n\t\tret.Param = arguments[0]\n\t}\n\n\tif len(arguments) != desiredArgs {\n\t\tp.addParseErrf(ret.PositionRange(), \"wrong number of arguments for aggregate expression provided, expected %d, got %d\", desiredArgs, len(arguments))\n\t\treturn ret\n\t}\n\n\tret.Expr = arguments[desiredArgs-1]\n\n\treturn ret\n}\n\n// newMap is used when building the FloatHistogram from a map.\nfunc (*parser) newMap() (ret map[string]any) {\n\treturn map[string]any{}\n}\n\n// mergeMaps is used to combine maps as they're used to later build the Float histogram.\n// This will merge the right map into the left map.\nfunc (p *parser) mergeMaps(left, right *map[string]any) (ret *map[string]any) {\n\tfor key, value := range *right {\n\t\tif _, ok := (*left)[key]; ok {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(posrange.PositionRange{}, \"duplicate key \\\"%s\\\" in histogram\", key)\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\t(*left)[key] = value\n\t}\n\treturn left\n}\n\nfunc (p *parser) histogramsIncreaseSeries(base, inc *histogram.FloatHistogram, times uint64) ([]SequenceValue, error) {\n\t// Capture the hint set flag immediately after inc histogram is built.\n\t// The base histogram's hint set flag was already captured.\n\thintSet := p.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet\n\treturn p.histogramsSeries(base, inc, times, hintSet, func(a, b *histogram.FloatHistogram) (*histogram.FloatHistogram, error) {\n\t\tres, _, _, err := a.Add(b)\n\t\treturn res, err\n\t})\n}\n\nfunc (p *parser) histogramsDecreaseSeries(base, inc *histogram.FloatHistogram, times uint64) ([]SequenceValue, error) {\n\t// Capture the hint set flag immediately after inc histogram is built.\n\thintSet := p.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet\n\treturn p.histogramsSeries(base, inc, times, hintSet, func(a, b *histogram.FloatHistogram) (*histogram.FloatHistogram, error) {\n\t\tres, _, _, err := a.Sub(b)\n\t\treturn res, err\n\t})\n}\n\nfunc (*parser) histogramsSeries(base, inc *histogram.FloatHistogram, times uint64, counterResetHintSet bool,\n\tcombine func(*histogram.FloatHistogram, *histogram.FloatHistogram) (*histogram.FloatHistogram, error),\n) ([]SequenceValue, error) {\n\tret := make([]SequenceValue, times+1)\n\t// Add an additional value (the base) for time 0, which we ignore in tests.\n\tret[0] = SequenceValue{Histogram: base, CounterResetHintSet: counterResetHintSet}\n\tcur := base\n\tfor i := uint64(1); i <= times; i++ {\n\t\tif cur.Schema > inc.Schema {\n\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"error combining histograms: cannot merge from schema %d to %d\", inc.Schema, cur.Schema)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tvar err error\n\t\tcur, err = combine(cur.Copy(), inc)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn ret, err\n\t\t}\n\t\tret[i] = SequenceValue{Histogram: cur, CounterResetHintSet: counterResetHintSet}\n\t}\n\n\treturn ret, nil\n}\n\n// buildHistogramFromMap is used in the grammar to take then individual parts of the histogram and complete it.\nfunc (p *parser) buildHistogramFromMap(desc *map[string]any) *histogram.FloatHistogram {\n\toutput := &histogram.FloatHistogram{}\n\t// Reset the flag for each new histogram being built.\n\tp.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet = false\n\n\tval, ok := (*desc)[\"schema\"]\n\tif ok {\n\t\tschema, ok := val.(int64)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\toutput.Schema = int32(schema)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing schema number: %v\", val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"sum\"]\n\tif ok {\n\t\tsum, ok := val.(float64)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\toutput.Sum = sum\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing sum number: %v\", val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"count\"]\n\tif ok {\n\t\tcount, ok := val.(float64)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\toutput.Count = count\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing count number: %v\", val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"z_bucket\"]\n\tif ok {\n\t\tbucket, ok := val.(float64)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\toutput.ZeroCount = bucket\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing z_bucket number: %v\", val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"z_bucket_w\"]\n\tif ok {\n\t\tbucketWidth, ok := val.(float64)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\toutput.ZeroThreshold = bucketWidth\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing z_bucket_w number: %v\", val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"custom_values\"]\n\tif ok {\n\t\tcustomValues, ok := val.([]float64)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\toutput.CustomValues = customValues\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing custom_values: %v\", val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tval, ok = (*desc)[\"counter_reset_hint\"]\n\tif ok {\n\t\t// Mark that the counter reset hint was explicitly specified.\n\t\tp.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet = true\n\t\tresetHint, ok := val.(Item)\n\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\tswitch resetHint.Typ {\n\t\t\tcase UNKNOWN_COUNTER_RESET:\n\t\t\t\toutput.CounterResetHint = histogram.UnknownCounterReset\n\t\t\tcase COUNTER_RESET:\n\t\t\t\toutput.CounterResetHint = histogram.CounterReset\n\t\t\tcase NOT_COUNTER_RESET:\n\t\t\t\toutput.CounterResetHint = histogram.NotCounterReset\n\t\t\tcase GAUGE_TYPE:\n\t\t\t\toutput.CounterResetHint = histogram.GaugeType\n\t\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing counter_reset_hint: unknown value %v\", resetHint.Typ)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing counter_reset_hint: %v\", val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tbuckets, spans := p.buildHistogramBucketsAndSpans(desc, \"buckets\", \"offset\")\n\toutput.PositiveBuckets = buckets\n\toutput.PositiveSpans = spans\n\n\tbuckets, spans = p.buildHistogramBucketsAndSpans(desc, \"n_buckets\", \"n_offset\")\n\toutput.NegativeBuckets = buckets\n\toutput.NegativeSpans = spans\n\n\treturn output\n}\n\n// newHistogramSequenceValue creates a SequenceValue for a histogram,\n// setting CounterResetHintSet based on whether counter_reset_hint was\n// explicitly specified in the histogram description.\nfunc (p *parser) newHistogramSequenceValue(h *histogram.FloatHistogram) SequenceValue {\n\treturn SequenceValue{\n\t\tHistogram:           h,\n\t\tCounterResetHintSet: p.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet,\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (p *parser) buildHistogramBucketsAndSpans(desc *map[string]any, bucketsKey, offsetKey string,\n) (buckets []float64, spans []histogram.Span) {\n\tbucketCount := 0\n\tval, ok := (*desc)[bucketsKey]\n\tif ok {\n\t\tval, ok := val.([]float64)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\tbuckets = val\n\t\t\tbucketCount = len(buckets)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing %s float array: %v\", bucketsKey, val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\toffset := int32(0)\n\tval, ok = (*desc)[offsetKey]\n\tif ok {\n\t\tval, ok := val.(int64)\n\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\toffset = int32(val)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing %s number: %v\", offsetKey, val)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tif bucketCount > 0 {\n\t\tspans = []histogram.Span{{Offset: offset, Length: uint32(bucketCount)}}\n\t}\n\treturn buckets, spans\n}\n\n// number parses a number.\nfunc (p *parser) number(val string) float64 {\n\tn, err := strconv.ParseInt(val, 0, 64)\n\tf := float64(n)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tf, err = strconv.ParseFloat(val, 64)\n\t}\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing number: %s\", err)\n\t}\n\treturn f\n}\n\n// expectType checks the type of the node and raises an error if it\n// is not of the expected type.\nfunc (p *parser) expectType(node Node, want ValueType, context string) {\n\tt := p.checkAST(node)\n\tif t != want {\n\t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"expected type %s in %s, got %s\", DocumentedType(want), context, DocumentedType(t))\n\t}\n}\n\n// checkAST checks the validity of the provided AST. This includes type checking.\nfunc (p *parser) checkAST(node Node) (typ ValueType) {\n\t// For expressions the type is determined by their Type function.\n\t// Lists do not have a type but are not invalid either.\n\tswitch n := node.(type) {\n\tcase Expressions:\n\t\ttyp = ValueTypeNone\n\tcase Expr:\n\t\ttyp = n.Type()\n\tdefault:\n\t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"unknown node type: %T\", node)\n\t}\n\n\t// Recursively check correct typing for child nodes and raise\n\t// errors in case of bad typing.\n\tswitch n := node.(type) {\n\tcase *EvalStmt:\n\t\tty := p.checkAST(n.Expr)\n\t\tif ty == ValueTypeNone {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.Expr.PositionRange(), \"evaluation statement must have a valid expression type but got %s\", DocumentedType(ty))\n\t\t}\n\n\tcase Expressions:\n\t\tfor _, e := range n {\n\t\t\tty := p.checkAST(e)\n\t\t\tif ty == ValueTypeNone {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(e.PositionRange(), \"expression must have a valid expression type but got %s\", DocumentedType(ty))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\tcase *AggregateExpr:\n\t\tif !n.Op.IsAggregator() {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"aggregation operator expected in aggregation expression but got %q\", n.Op)\n\t\t}\n\t\tp.expectType(n.Expr, ValueTypeVector, \"aggregation expression\")\n\t\tif n.Op == TOPK || n.Op == BOTTOMK || n.Op == QUANTILE || n.Op == LIMITK || n.Op == LIMIT_RATIO {\n\t\t\tp.expectType(n.Param, ValueTypeScalar, \"aggregation parameter\")\n\t\t}\n\t\tif n.Op == COUNT_VALUES {\n\t\t\tp.expectType(n.Param, ValueTypeString, \"aggregation parameter\")\n\t\t}\n\n\tcase *BinaryExpr:\n\t\tlt := p.checkAST(n.LHS)\n\t\trt := p.checkAST(n.RHS)\n\n\t\t// opRange returns the PositionRange of the operator part of the BinaryExpr.\n\t\t// This is made a function instead of a variable, so it is lazily evaluated on demand.\n\t\topRange := func() (r posrange.PositionRange) {\n\t\t\t// Remove whitespace at the beginning and end of the range.\n\t\t\tfor r.Start = n.LHS.PositionRange().End; isSpace(rune(p.lex.input[r.Start])); r.Start++ {\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tfor r.End = n.RHS.PositionRange().Start - 1; isSpace(rune(p.lex.input[r.End])); r.End-- {\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn r\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif n.ReturnBool && !n.Op.IsComparisonOperator() {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"bool modifier can only be used on comparison operators\")\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif n.Op.IsComparisonOperator() && !n.ReturnBool && n.RHS.Type() == ValueTypeScalar && n.LHS.Type() == ValueTypeScalar {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"comparisons between scalars must use BOOL modifier\")\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif n.Op.IsSetOperator() && n.VectorMatching.Card == CardOneToOne {\n\t\t\tn.VectorMatching.Card = CardManyToMany\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tfor _, l1 := range n.VectorMatching.MatchingLabels {\n\t\t\tfor _, l2 := range n.VectorMatching.Include {\n\t\t\t\tif l1 == l2 && n.VectorMatching.On {\n\t\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"label %q must not occur in ON and GROUP clause at once\", l1)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif !n.Op.IsOperator() {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"binary expression does not support operator %q\", n.Op)\n\t\t}\n\t\tif lt != ValueTypeScalar && lt != ValueTypeVector {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.LHS.PositionRange(), \"binary expression must contain only scalar and instant vector types\")\n\t\t}\n\t\tif rt != ValueTypeScalar && rt != ValueTypeVector {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.RHS.PositionRange(), \"binary expression must contain only scalar and instant vector types\")\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tswitch {\n\t\tcase (lt != ValueTypeVector || rt != ValueTypeVector) && n.VectorMatching != nil:\n\t\t\tif len(n.VectorMatching.MatchingLabels) > 0 {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"vector matching only allowed between instant vectors\")\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.FillValues.LHS != nil || n.VectorMatching.FillValues.RHS != nil {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"filling in missing series only allowed between instant vectors\")\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tn.VectorMatching = nil\n\t\tcase n.Op.IsSetOperator(): // Both operands are Vectors.\n\t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.Card == CardOneToMany || n.VectorMatching.Card == CardManyToOne {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"no grouping allowed for %q operation\", n.Op)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.Card != CardManyToMany {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"set operations must always be many-to-many\")\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.FillValues.LHS != nil || n.VectorMatching.FillValues.RHS != nil {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"filling in missing series not allowed for set operators\")\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif (lt == ValueTypeScalar || rt == ValueTypeScalar) && n.Op.IsSetOperator() {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"set operator %q not allowed in binary scalar expression\", n.Op)\n\t\t}\n\n\tcase *Call:\n\t\tnargs := len(n.Func.ArgTypes)\n\t\tif n.Func.Variadic == 0 {\n\t\t\tif nargs != len(n.Args) {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"expected %d argument(s) in call to %q, got %d\", nargs, n.Func.Name, len(n.Args))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tna := nargs - 1\n\t\t\tif na > len(n.Args) {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"expected at least %d argument(s) in call to %q, got %d\", na, n.Func.Name, len(n.Args))\n\t\t\t} else if nargsmax := na + n.Func.Variadic; n.Func.Variadic > 0 && nargsmax < len(n.Args) {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"expected at most %d argument(s) in call to %q, got %d\", nargsmax, n.Func.Name, len(n.Args))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif n.Func.Name == \"info\" && len(n.Args) > 1 {\n\t\t\t// Check the type is correct first\n\t\t\tif n.Args[1].Type() != ValueTypeVector {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"expected type %s in %s, got %s\", DocumentedType(ValueTypeVector), fmt.Sprintf(\"call to function %q\", n.Func.Name), DocumentedType(n.Args[1].Type()))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t// Check the vector selector in the input doesn't contain a metric name\n\t\t\tif vs, ok := n.Args[1].(*VectorSelector); ok && vs.Name != \"\" {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.Args[1].PositionRange(), \"expected label selectors only, got vector selector instead\")\n\t\t\t} else if ok {\n\t\t\t\t// Set Vector Selector flag to bypass empty matcher check\n\t\t\t\tvs.BypassEmptyMatcherCheck = true\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.Args[1].PositionRange(), \"expected label selectors only\")\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tfor i, arg := range n.Args {\n\t\t\tif i >= len(n.Func.ArgTypes) {\n\t\t\t\tif n.Func.Variadic == 0 {\n\t\t\t\t\t// This is not a vararg function so we should not check the\n\t\t\t\t\t// type of the extra arguments.\n\t\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\ti = len(n.Func.ArgTypes) - 1\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif t := p.checkAST(arg); t != n.Func.ArgTypes[i] {\n\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(arg.PositionRange(), \"expected type %s in call to function %q, got %s\", DocumentedType(n.Func.ArgTypes[i]), n.Func.Name, DocumentedType(t))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\tcase *ParenExpr:\n\t\tp.checkAST(n.Expr)\n\n\tcase *UnaryExpr:\n\t\tif n.Op != ADD && n.Op != SUB {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"only + and - operators allowed for unary expressions\")\n\t\t}\n\t\tif t := p.checkAST(n.Expr); t != ValueTypeScalar && t != ValueTypeVector {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"unary expression only allowed on expressions of type scalar or instant vector, got %q\", DocumentedType(t))\n\t\t}\n\n\tcase *SubqueryExpr:\n\t\tty := p.checkAST(n.Expr)\n\t\tif ty != ValueTypeVector {\n\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"subquery is only allowed on instant vector, got %s instead\", ty)\n\t\t}\n\tcase *MatrixSelector:\n\t\tp.checkAST(n.VectorSelector)\n\n\tcase *VectorSelector:\n\t\tif n.Name != \"\" {\n\t\t\t// In this case the last LabelMatcher is checking for the metric name\n\t\t\t// set outside the braces. FunctionCall is the type of a PromQL function implementation\n//\n// vals is a list of the evaluated arguments for the function call.\n//\n// For range vectors it will be a Matrix with one series, The vectors in vals should not be returned.a\n//\n// Range vector functions need only return a vector with the right value,\n// the metric and timestamp are not needed.\n//\n// Instant vector value at the left boundary of the range.\n// If interpolation is needed (when smoothed is true and the first sample is before the range start),\n// it returns the interpolated value at the left boundary; otherwise, it returns the first sample's value.\nfunc pickOrInterpolateLeft(floats []FPoint, first int, rangeStart int64, smoothed, isCounter bool) float64 {\n\tif smoothed && floats[first].T < rangeStart {\n\t\treturn interpolate(floats[first], floats[first+1], rangeStart, isCounter)\n\t}\n\treturn floats[first].F\n}\n\n// pickOrInterpolateRight returns the value at the right boundary of the range.\n// If interpolation is needed (when smoothed is true and the last sample is after the range end),\n// it returns the interpolated value at the right boundary; otherwise, it returns the last sample's value.\nfunc pickOrInterpolateRight(floats []FPoint, last int, rangeEnd int64, smoothed, isCounter bool) float64 {\n\tif smoothed && last > 0 && floats[last].T > rangeEnd {\n\t\treturn interpolate(floats[last-1], floats[last], rangeEnd, isCounter)\n\t}\n\treturn floats[last].F\n}\n\n// interpolate performs linear interpolation between two points.\n// If isCounter is true and there is a counter reset, it models the counter\n// as starting from 0 (post-reset) by setting y1 to 0.\n// It then calculates the interpolated value at the given timestamp.\nfunc interpolate(p1, p2 FPoint, t int64, isCounter bool) float64 {\n\ty1 := p1.F\n\ty2 := p2.F\n\tif isCounter && y2 < y1 {\n\t\ty1 = 0\n\t}\n\n\treturn y1 + (y2-y1)*float64(t-p1.T)/float64(p2.T-p1.T)\n}\n\n// correctForCounterResets calculates the correction for counter resets.\n// This function is only used for extendedRate functions with smoothed or anchored rates.\nfunc correctForCounterResets(left, right float64, points []FPoint) float64 {\n\tvar correction float64\n\tprev := left\n\tfor _, p := range points {\n\t\tif p.F < prev {\n\t\t\tcorrection += prev\n\t\t}\n\t\tprev = p.F\n\t}\n\tif right < prev {\n\t\tcorrection += prev\n\t}\n\treturn correction\n}\n\n// extendedRate is a utility function for anchored/smoothed rate/increase/delta.\n// It calculates the rate (allowing for counter resets if isCounter is true),\n// extrapolates if the first/last sample if needed, and returns\n// the result as either per-second (if isRate is true) or overall.\nfunc extendedRate(vals Matrix, args parser.Expressions, enh *EvalNodeHelper, isCounter, isRate bool) (Vector, annotations.Annotations) {\n\tvar (\n\t\tms              = args[0].(*parser.MatrixSelector)\n\t\tvs              = ms.VectorSelector.(*parser.VectorSelector)\n\t\tsamples         = vals[0]\n\t\tf               = samples.Floats\n\t\tlastSampleIndex = len(f) - 1\n\t\trangeStart      = enh.Ts - durationMilliseconds(ms.Range+vs.Offset)\n\t\trangeEnd        = enh.Ts - durationMilliseconds(vs.Offset)\n\t\tannos           annotations.Annotations\n\t\tsmoothed        = vs.Smoothed\n\t)\n\n\tfirstSampleIndex := max(0, sort.Search(lastSampleIndex, func(i int) bool { return f[i].T > rangeStart })-1)\n\tif smoothed {\n\t\tlastSampleIndex = sort.Search(lastSampleIndex, func(i int) bool { return f[i].T >= rangeEnd })\n\t}\n\n\tif f[lastSampleIndex].T <= rangeStart {\n\t\treturn enh.Out, annos\n\t}\n\n\tleft := pickOrInterpolateLeft(f,
